It is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المَيِّتَ يُعَذَّبُ بِبُكَآءِ أَهْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Verily the dead will be punished for his family's weeping for him</hi>]: the reason of which is probably this; that the Arabs used to charge their families to weep and wail for them; therefore the dead is obnoxious to punishment for his having done this.                   </form> [for <foreign lang="ar">خَمْرٌ مُعَذَّبَةٌ</foreign>] <hi rend="ital">Wine mixed</hi> [<hi rend="ital">with water,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with some other thing</hi> or <hi rend="ital">things</hi>]. (A, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">معذب</foreign> [app. <foreign lang="ar">مُعَذَّب</foreign>] is applied by the vulgar to Fresh ripe dates <hi rend="ital">soaked with water.</hi> (TA voce <foreign lang="ar">مَنْقُوشٌ</foreign>.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">سَوْطٌ مُعَذَّبٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A whip having an</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عِلَاقَة</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">عَذَبَة</foreign>] <hi rend="ital">attached to it.</hi> (TA.)
